    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1001083523" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1001083523" />
    <a title="Conor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30552336-conor"><img alt="Conor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400278909p2/30552336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1001083523?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Conor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Conor" href="/user/show/30552336-conor">Conor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30552336-conor?shelf=awesome-books-are-awesome">awesome-books-are-awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1001083523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1778864837410745928">4.5 Stars.<br/><br/>New setting. New characters. New conflict. Still awesome. <br/><br/>After spending 4 massive books developing one of the deepest and most immersive settings in fantasy, establishing one of the largest and most diverse casts of characters and setting up machinations of incredible complexity and scope…Erikson starts all over again. For all that I missed the character and settings I’ve come to love in this series their replacements in this book were great and while I found the start to be a bit slo</span>
  <span id="freeText1778864837410745928" style="display:none">4.5 Stars.<br /><br />New setting. New characters. New conflict. Still awesome. <br /><br />After spending 4 massive books developing one of the deepest and most immersive settings in fantasy, establishing one of the largest and most diverse casts of characters and setting up machinations of incredible complexity and scope…Erikson starts all over again. For all that I missed the character and settings I’ve come to love in this series their replacements in this book were great and while I found the start to be a bit slow (although not as much as many of my friends seem to have) the story as a whole was really enjoyable, capped with possibly the strongest finale in the series to date. <br /><br />I really liked the balance of the POV structure of this book, something that’s been hit and miss in this series so far. The chapters alternate in focus between the two major cultures with every other chapter featuring the POV’s of one of the two sets of main characters. I found the Tiste Edur to be a really interesting, well-developed culture with a cool mixture of Native American customs (counting coup), mysterious magic and ancient secrets. However at the start I struggled to care about the two main characters the Edur storyline revolved around, the slave Udinaas and the conscience-burdened warrior Trull. While I cared more about them as the book progressed and their storylines become more interesting they’re still nowhere near my favourites in the series. I was also really frustrated at how the Edur plot developed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ when Rhulad, a previously untried warrior returned mysteriously from death horrendously deformed and obviously insane and was able to violate all of the Edur’s ferociously guarded, millenia old customs and declare himself emperor with no one even trying to oppose him. I found this to be really unbelievable and a pretty lazy set up for Trull’s lone rebel story arc.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> However I did really like how Rhulad was written throughout. At the start he was seemingly set up to be a Joffrey-like irredeemable dickhead but through his interactions with Trull and especially Udinaas he is shown in a much more sympathetic light as a tortured young man genuinely trying to do what he feels is right. <br /><br />The other main storyline examined the Letherii Empire. I found this setting to be incredibly annoying. Throughout the book Erikson litters Letherii culture with constant parallels to modern capitalism. At first I wasn’t a fan of this due to it feeling out of place in a fantasy setting and the missed opportunity of a more traditional civilisation vs. barbarians dynamic such as Karsa’s story in HoC. However these problems soon paled in comparison to my frustration at Erikson’s constant, ham-fisted vilification of capitalism and western/American culture. The Edur characters naturally refer to their enemies with hatred and disgust but even the Letherii characters (at least the good guys) express at best apathy and at worst hatred towards their own culture. This became even more frustrating when Erikson hinted at the cultures surrounding the Letherii: The mournful people of Bluerose, survivors of an ancient war. The Tarthenal, giants descended from a powerful, advanced race now reduced to barbarism as their culture decays around them. The Nerek, whose fervent belief in their goddess, an earth mother avatar, can’t be dimmed even by oppression and servitude. Even by his high standards Erikson created some incredibly fascinating cultures… Before immediately going back to a ‘Capitalism is really bad you guys’ lecture. What was really incredible about this contrast was that Erikson created these intriguing cultures based on a few throwaway lines, leaving the reader to fill in the world-building dots themselves whereas with the Letherii he dedicates several paragraphs of awkwardly tacked-on rambling philosophy about how evil they are. Every. Single. Chapter (punctuation for emphasis well-deserved). Note: I realise this is pretty much a long rant about Erikson’s long rants about politics. Irony can be a bitch.<br /><br />Setting aside the setting I loved the Letherii sections. Unlike the Edur they had great central characters in the form of the two Beddict brothers. Brys, the master swordsman, is a typical fantasy character written with great deftness and empathy. Tehol, a financial genius, is a much more unorthodox character. While I didn’t understand all of the hype around him at first he quickly grew on me and his hilarious dialogue with his droll manservant Bugg were some of the book’s highlights. They were surrounded by a cast of great supporting characters as well: The aforementioned Bugg, manservant, healer, priest, feared by demons and worshipped by refugees as ‘The Waiting Man’. Shurq, the undead nymphomaniac thief (no, really). The Ceda, an eccentric, hilarious and extremely powerful mage. I thought that both the machinations of the court and Tehol’s financial schemes were really well done. <br /><br />The last main POV character was Seren Pedac who serves as a conduit between the two warring cultures, both as a narrative device separate from the two pairs of POV’s and in the story. At the beginning I found her to be somewhat dull and uninteresting. However her story took a horrific turn halfway through that made me feel a lot more sympathetic towards her and shortly afterwards her story became much more interesting as she joined up with The Crimson Guard. Erikson again demonstrated his brilliance at writing intriguing cultures and again did so with a minimalist approach. At the end of the book we still don’t know much but what we do know is that 1) The Crimson Guard are badass 2) The Avowed are really badass 3) Skinner (who doesn’t even appear in this one despite being name-dropped a load of times, often in unexpected places leading to him now being probably the fantasy character I most want to know more about) is really, really badass. I especially liked Iron Bars (who's awesomeness has already been suitably covered in many of my friends reviews) and Corlo as characters. <br /><br />I was somewhat disappointed with how the Edur-Letherii conflict ultimately played out. I’ve mentioned a number of times before how OP magic can be compared to armies in this series but it never played as prominent a role as in this book. The Letherii were established as a massive nation, with a powerful economy and a huge, highly professional army that had a level of sophistication in terms of strategy and doctrine that probably wouldn’t be seen irl until WW1 and yet they were completely helpless against the Edur magic that pretty much came out of nowhere <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ From what I understand their main source of power is the Crippled God but isn’t he 1) Crippled and thus nor at full strength and 2) Kind of pre-occupied with all of the incredibly complex schemes he’s been masterminding over the last few books.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> While this was addressed to some extent it was done only at the very end in a couple of lines and never looked at again. I hope the rest of the series will explore the magic&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;everything else continuity error more as at the minute it’s probably my biggest (only?) long standing complaint about the series. My disappointment with the conflict left me with a sour taste about this book that was however quickly forgotten due to the awesome ending. Erikson has written some great endings in this series but for me this was the strongest to date. <br /><br />This was a difficult book to rate. There were a number of annoying features (Rhulad's rise to power, Erikson's constant capitalism is evil schtick) but there were also a number of awesome features (great characters in the Letherii plot, some really cool cultures, the Crimson Guard and an epic ending). Ultimately though the good far outweighed the bad in this one and I’m now really psyched to get back to the main setting and see how the events of this book tie into the rest of the series. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1778864837410745928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1877172119" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1877172119" />
    <a title="Michael Britt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt"><img alt="Michael Britt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513347398p2/51188905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1877172119?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Britt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Britt" href="/user/show/51188905-michael-britt">Michael Britt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780765316516" href="/book/show/55402.Midnight_Tides">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1877172119" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer930587931508882417">Once again, I'll keep this review as spoiler-free as possible. I definitely won't put any big spoilers in it.<br/><br/>Don't let the amount of time it took me to finish this book fool you: this is yet another amazing installment in the Malazan series. Up to this book, we've been introduced to a enormous cast of characters. And this book adds a completely new cast of characters, Trull Sengar is the only familiar face we see. Some may be turned off by this, but you quickly get used to it and everyone become</span>
  <span id="freeText930587931508882417" style="display:none">Once again, I'll keep this review as spoiler-free as possible. I definitely won't put any big spoilers in it.<br /><br />Don't let the amount of time it took me to finish this book fool you: this is yet another amazing installment in the Malazan series. Up to this book, we've been introduced to a enormous cast of characters. And this book adds a completely new cast of characters, Trull Sengar is the only familiar face we see. Some may be turned off by this, but you quickly get used to it and everyone becomes as well known as the previous cast. I think I didn't mind this due to how much I loved so many of these characters. You can really tell that Erickson is honing his craft more and more with each new book. He continues to excel in his ability to give us some great characters. You really love the characters he meant for us to love, and hate the ones you're supposed to hate. Although, I still felt a pang of sympathy for one of the characters that we're meant to hate. There really wasn't that many battle scenes, but the ones we did get were so well executed. I can't think of any author who writes more brutal battle scenes without it feeling like he's going over the top. <br /><br />The characters I came to love most were definitely Tehol and Bugg. Their comic relief and witty banter were thoroughly enjoyable. I found myself actually laughing out loud at quite a few of their scenes, and if I wasn't laughing, I had a huge grin on my face. Besides that, I think Bugg is one of the most intriguing characters yet. You can really tell that we're not getting all the info on Bugg, that we're being kept out of the loop on something. Without giving anything away, I think we're going to see some amazing scenes come from future Bugg. <br /><br />The Sengar family had a pretty interesting story arc as well. There's not really much I can say about them without going into spoiler territory. But it was pretty fun to see the split in the family regarding one of the big conflicts in this story. I thought we were going to get to see what made the events transpire in the prologue of House of Chains, so I was pretty disappointed when the ending didn't lead into that. I imagine we'll see that soon enough, though. I think we can infer why HoC's prologue happens, but I was hoping to see the real reason. <br /><br />The Letherii side of the story had so many interesting characters, as well. Obviously Tehol and Bugg, but also people like Ublala Pung, Kettle, Shurq Elalle, and one of my newest favorites, Iron Bars. <br /><br />All-in-all, yet another amazing installment in the Malazan series. Now, onto Bonehunters!</span>
  <a data-text-id="930587931508882417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2168856291" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2168856291" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2168856291?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2168856291" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer217611081916699415"><b>
  <i>Death is every mortal's shadow, his true shadow, and time is its servant, spinning that shadow slowly round, until what stretched behind one now stretches before him.</i>
</b><br/><br/>To say I was sceptical to read this book is an understatement, I was so scared, I thought I might not like this cause I know that this will be filled with completely new characters, location, world, it was like starting a whole new series. But I was so wrong, I loved it, I must admit it was hard to get into, not as hard as GoTM </span>
  <span id="freeText217611081916699415" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Death is every mortal's shadow, his true shadow, and time is its servant, spinning that shadow slowly round, until what stretched behind one now stretches before him.</i>
</b><br /><br />To say I was sceptical to read this book is an understatement, I was so scared, I thought I might not like this cause I know that this will be filled with completely new characters, location, world, it was like starting a whole new series. But I was so wrong, I loved it, I must admit it was hard to get into, not as hard as GoTM but still hard. I can totally see the connection between this book and the previous in the series, can’t wait for when they all meet. Like all books in this series, this book has a good dose of friendship, amazing battle scenes, malazan kind of romance that is usually tragic, diversity, family etc, there is basically nothing missing in this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>'Civilization after civilization, it is the same. The world falls to tyranny with a whisper. The frightened are ever keen to bow to a perceived necessity, in the belief that necessity forces conformity, and conformity a certain stability.</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>Before starting this book it is important to note this two things, it took me a while to know what they were.<br />1. This is Trull Sengar’s story, these events happened before HoC, it happened at the same time with GotM. They are also other POVs that helped made the story more understandable. So yes the Crippled god have being interfering long before most people realized.<br />2.The Hold, this was mentioned basically almost throughout the book, I thought it meant the Deck of Dragons but no its not. The Hold of Tiles is an older version of the Deck of Dragons that Elder gods uses.</i><br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />Steven Erikson still manages to improve in his already perfect world building, there is so much improvement between this and the previous books, same goes for the writing, no longer a million POVs but a few that is comprehensible and tell the story well. I only wish the dialogue was more than the internal monologue.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The new plaster isn't showing any cracks. The owners are delighted—'<br />'I thought I owned those warehouses.'<br />'Aren't you delighted?'<br />'Well, you're right, I am. Every one of me.'</i>
</b><br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />My favourite part of the book, I love a good character driven books, especially when its well written and depicted. Two major races are the focus of this book. The Tiste Edur and the Letherii.<br /><br /><b>The Tiste Edur</b><br />The Sengar brothers which include my personal favourite <i>Trull Sengar</i> the only known character, Udinaas, their Letherii slave, Mayen, Hanan Mosag and a host of others.<br /><br />Trull Sengar’s story is even sadder than I anticipated, he is such a great man, kind, humble, honourable etc, he is never afraid to voice his opinions and doubts, despite the repercussions, and that was what lead to him being shorned by his people. I wish he was the eldest of the four brothers, things would have gone better for them, but no he is the second out of four sons.<br /><br />Fear Sengar is the first son, I seriously have no idea what to make of him at first, the guy has almost no facial expressions, he is the definition of impassive, ever the perfect warrior, how I wish he listens to Trull instead of shutting him up. When he finally started questioning things it was almost too late, I hope its not too late.<br /><br />Binadas Sengar is the third Sengar brother, also the only sorcerer among them, the guy is so sceptical and evasive that I still don’t know what to make of him.<br /><br />Rhulad Sengar the fourth and last son, I neither love nor hate him, I just pity him. He is not exactly a good guy but he doesn’t deserve what is happening to him, no one does, hope his brothers will find a solution.<br /><br />Udinaas is a slave at the Sengar household, I really felt for him, everyone was just using him, not only mortals but other worldly creatures, I hope things gets better for him, he deserves more.<br /><br /><br /><b>The Letherii</b><br />Which include the Beddict brothers, Seren Pedac, Shurq Elalle, Kettle,Bugg, Ublala Pung, Shand, Rissari, Hesun and others.<br /><br />Tehol Beddict is the second and middle son among the Beddict brothers. The guy is a mystery, he walks around with bedsheet tied around his waist or a woollen trousers of grey and yellow colour, not to mention he sleeps on his roof. Tehol is also a genius, even the Queen despise him because of something he did in the past, he is not a fighter, am pretty sure he doesn’t know how to use a sword, he is also kind and honourable. His relationship with Bugg his manservant is one of my favourite things in this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Even genius has its flaws.'<br />Another grin. 'Even with you, Tehol?'<br />'Well, I was generalizing to put you at ease. I never include myself in my own generalizations. I am ever the exception to the rule.'<br />'And how do you manage that?'<br />'Well, I define the rules, of course. That's my particular game, brother.'</i>
</b><br /><br /><br />Brys Beddict the third Beddict brother is presently the king’s champion, like his brother Tehol he is also honourable, but a much better swordsman.<br /><br />Hull Beddict, the eldest of the three, he didn’t have a POV, so it was hard to know what goes on in his head, from what people said about him, he seems like a good man.<br /><br />Seren Pedac is a Aquitor, some kind of guide and travel agent, she guides people that goes to the Edur land. I love her, she isn’t exactly badass but she can hold herself in a fight, she is also feminine.<br /><br />Shurq Elalle is the opposite of Seren, she is an undead thief, even though she is undead she still steals, its quite ironic, she has very crazy friends, some undead like her others not so much.<br /><br /><b>
  <i><br />'I want to be scary. It's important that I be scary. I've been practising hissing and snarling.'<br />'No need for concern there,' Bugg replied. 'You'll be truly terrifying.<br />'If I eat human flesh,' Harlest said, 'it will rot in my stomach, won't it? That means I will stink. I like that. I like thinking about things like that. The smell of doom.'</i>
</b><br /><br />Silchas Ruin is an ascendent and soletaken who is Anomander’s younger brother, but unlike his brothers and race he is white skinned due to his albinism.</span>
  <a data-text-id="217611081916699415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_416454820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416454820" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416454820?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416454820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12699878037337983370">Problems with the book: <br/><br/>Everybody is a philosopher, every single person with POV. The usual structure of the book is the following: 5 pager worth of philosophical inner thoughts of a character following by 1 page of some action; I do not mean kick-the-crap-out-of-everybody action, just the acts of doing something, like mending a net. By my estimate, the book can be shortened by at least 2/3 by cutting on inner thoughts of secondary characters.<br/><br/>No matter what the author says, this is not a part of</span>
  <span id="freeText12699878037337983370" style="display:none">Problems with the book: <br /><br />Everybody is a philosopher, every single person with POV. The usual structure of the book is the following: 5 pager worth of philosophical inner thoughts of a character following by 1 page of some action; I do not mean kick-the-crap-out-of-everybody action, just the acts of doing something, like mending a net. By my estimate, the book can be shortened by at least 2/3 by cutting on inner thoughts of secondary characters.<br /><br />No matter what the author says, this is not a part of the series, this is a standalone book. Only one character from this book appears in the earlier books (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55398.House_of_Chains__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___4_" title="House of Chains (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #4) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a> to be exact). I failed to make any emotional connection with him even after finishing this book despite the fact that this was supposed to be his tragic life story. From looking into the list of characters of the next book, I see that only 3 of them (including the original guy) make it from this one; definitely not enough to warrant 700+ page book. New races, new places, even the magic system is different; so what exactly makes this book a part of Malazan series?<br /><br />Speaking of being able to connect to characters, I found I could only relate to one of them, and he does not get a lot of screen time (Iron Bars). A lot of people love Tehol, but I found him to be pointless to the story and not very believable. <br /><br />The book has strong anti-capitalistic undertones. I am not exactly the biggest fan of capitalism, but I really hate then something keeps hammering the message over and over; this is exactly what this book does. I got it already, please stop!<br /><br />The plot: two races want to start a war with each other. It is not clear what kept them from doing this earlier as there is no love lost between them, plus they want resources of their enemies. So this whole book is basically preparations for the war by these nations, or rather a lot of philosophical ramblings interrupted by the preparations. The actual war takes place in the last two chapters. <br /><br />2.5 stars; I really hate giving this rating to the series I really like, but this book made me take a break from reading not just the series, but fantasy genre in general.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12699878037337983370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/857542035?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857542035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3313279047628990586">I think the must be the third or fourth time i've read this book, but the first time i've ever taken the time to really read it. Previously, i'd approached it with little enthusiasm and more than a little petulance- why is this important? Why is it set before the first 4 books? Where are my favourite characters? Who cares about the Tiste Edur? A whole novel about Trull Sengar-are you serious? Thanks to this bad attitude, I skimmed the whole thing. I gave it 5 stars before because it's Erikson an</span>
  <span id="freeText3313279047628990586" style="display:none">I think the must be the third or fourth time i've read this book, but the first time i've ever taken the time to really read it. Previously, i'd approached it with little enthusiasm and more than a little petulance- why is this important? Why is it set before the first 4 books? Where are my favourite characters? Who cares about the Tiste Edur? A whole novel about Trull Sengar-are you serious? Thanks to this bad attitude, I skimmed the whole thing. I gave it 5 stars before because it's Erikson and no other reason. <br /><br />This time I give them freely, with full confidence and sincerity. I READ the book. And after the first few chapters of Trull whining, it was worth the effort. This instalment is Erikson doing political intrigue up close and personal. Of course, high politics underlies the entirety of the series, but the focus on the common man evens it out. Here, we get the power politics and economics of two clashing forces in direct opposition. It's done so very well through two trios of brothers: Sengar and Beddict. And this is where the new favourite characters come in: Tehol and Bugg. Love them or hate them, they lift intrigue to a different (rooftop) level. Not only that, i'd always passed over the Crimson Guard. I didn't even remember they were in this book. I defy anyone not to properly laugh out loud at Iron Bars' commentary. I'd love to quote it but it's too spoilery, those who've read it will already know anyway and those yet to read will know when they get there. There are more but again: SPOILERS.<br /><br />So all that i'll say is: don't make my mistake, trust in Erikson, the payoff is there for those that pay attention.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_313279450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313279450" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313279450?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313279450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3466103240976746325">This was another fantastic instalment in the Malazan series. I think it stands alongside House of Chains and Gardens of the Moon in terms of quality and perhaps only behind Memories of Ice as my favourite in the series. Erikson's stories can sometimes get a bit to grim and bleak for my liking, but I thought this one found the perfect balance. We had betrayal, tragedy, evil characters, and pain and suffering aplenty, but we also got likeable characters, friendship and loyalty, humour, and some ki</span>
  <span id="freeText3466103240976746325" style="display:none">This was another fantastic instalment in the Malazan series. I think it stands alongside House of Chains and Gardens of the Moon in terms of quality and perhaps only behind Memories of Ice as my favourite in the series. Erikson's stories can sometimes get a bit to grim and bleak for my liking, but I thought this one found the perfect balance. We had betrayal, tragedy, evil characters, and pain and suffering aplenty, but we also got likeable characters, friendship and loyalty, humour, and some kick-ass moments of noble deeds. <br /><br />Story wise we had some big changes in this one. A new continent, new problems, and only a handful of familiar characters. The action took place on the continent of Lether and focused on the impending clash between the Tiste Edur tribes and the kingdom of Lether. Neither culture was one to admire but Erikson succeed in making me interested in the conflict and in making my sympathize with a number of characters on each side. <br /><br />The kingdom of Lethar embodied all the worst elements of a modern capitalist society. The Edur reflected the evils of a society driven by the certainties of religion and nationalism. Erikson put the boot into both hard and often. Not done there he also managed to use the ensuing epic battles between the nations to decry the horrors of modern warfare. I can see why Erikson's musings may have upset some readers since they were not exactly subtle, but since I happen to agree with him they were not an issue for me. <br /><br />Which brings me to a personal favourite moment. A chat between Tehol and Bugg where Bugg is railing about the problems of the Letharii way of governance. Tehol asks Bugg how it could be done better and Bugg basically just tells him he has no idea and that human nature is what it is so it likely will always have issues with greed and corruption. A bleak view for sure, but another I find myself agreeing with. <br /><br />As with all Malazan books we got a mix of mortals and gods. We got to learn more of the Tiste Edur and the Tiste Andii and their entrance into this realm so long ago and we got to meet a bunch of their awesome Gods. Silchas Ruin, brother of Anomander Rake was the most notable, but we met plenty of others as well. We got another glimpse of the Crippled God and saw him setting a few of his plans into action. Then we had everything from Jaghut, Forkrul Assail, and demons, to Toblaki and Soletaken Gods making an appearance. <br /><br />We meet a host of great new characters. Most of the story revolved around the fates on the four Tiste Edur Sengar brothers and the three Letharii Beddict brothers. Erikson did a great job with both families. We had characters to love and despise and others who were deserving of a bit of both of those feelings. I was pretty happy with the story arcs for the all of them. The brothers aside we met a bunch of fun new characters like Iron Bars and Corlo from the famed Crimson Guard( I want more of them soon ), the hilarious and likeable undead trio of Shurq Elalle, Kettle, and Harlast( I hope we definitely see the female pair again ), The half Tarthanal Ublala Pung( So unlike Karsa!), Seren Pedac( I did not love her, but I suspect her future will make for interesting reading), and the Letharii slave Udinaas( a hard character to figure out but I found myself mostly sympathizing with the guy). I've likely forgot a few, but that is the way of things when you have such a large and interesting cast! <br /><br />I found the pacing of the story to be very good and I was totally caught up in the engaging tale. I was dreading the ending, but Erikson pulled off a satisfactory one in the midst of another epic and exciting convergence.<br /><br />I cannot wait to read what happens next. Things bode well for the Bonehunters being an awesome read.<br /><br />Rating: 5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Micheal Page did an excellent job with the narration of Midnight Tides. It helped that the cast was completely different so the inconsistencies between Page and Lister character interpretations was a non-issue. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3466103240976746325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2482842917" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2482842917" />
    <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan"><img alt="Graeme Rodaughan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464911366p2/56397934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2482842917?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Graeme Rodaughan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Graeme Rodaughan" href="/user/show/56397934-graeme-rodaughan">Graeme Rodaughan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of Epic Fantasy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=dark-fantasy-book-series">dark-fantasy-book-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=shapeshifters">shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=sorcerors-magicians">sorcerors-magicians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56397934-graeme-rodaughan?shelf=heroic-fantasy">heroic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2482842917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7341618341685455275"><b>Another monster epic of a book in the amazing Malazan Book of the Fallen series.</b><br/><br/>I'm in awe of Steven Erikson's story telling ability. He handles a vast array of characters with a deft touch that blows my mind with how seamless and varied his characterization is.<br/><br/>A direct parallel to his characterization skills is his ability to weave multiple narrative threads together into a seamless (there's that word again) whole that is both logically coherent (no plot holes) and arranged for powerful emotion</span>
  <span id="freeText7341618341685455275" style="display:none"><b>Another monster epic of a book in the amazing Malazan Book of the Fallen series.</b><br /><br />I'm in awe of Steven Erikson's story telling ability. He handles a vast array of characters with a deft touch that blows my mind with how seamless and varied his characterization is.<br /><br />A direct parallel to his characterization skills is his ability to weave multiple narrative threads together into a seamless (there's that word again) whole that is both logically coherent (no plot holes) and arranged for powerful emotional effect.<br /><br />This is super-cool writing.<br /><br />I've got a sneaking suspicion that some of the characters could provide more insight than my gushing fanboying, so let's ask them.<br /><br />Fear Sengar: "I signed up for a role titled, 'Brave Sengar,' so what's up with that?"<br /><br />Trull Sengar: "Playing the role of the honest, non-conformist in a society governed by strict adherence to a set of false beliefs, has been quite the challenge. I had to dig deep emotionally to make it through this story. I might need a holiday, perhaps down at a beach, a bit of peace and quiet. Maybe I'll go on a long walk afterward."<br /><br />Rhulad Sengar: "Hey, all I wanted was a little respect. Was that asking for too much? Geez, (shakes head dolefully, sighs) whoever said, 'heavy lies the crown,' was not wrong."<br /><br />Hannan Mosag: "Next time I'm using napalm and nukes, that'll frak them right up!"<br /><br />Udinass: "I nominated myself for the 'best friend,' award but kinda messed it up. My goodness, it got confusing there at the end. I didn't know if I was coming or going, of who I was with, or was I alone, sheesh!"<br /><br />Brys Beddict: "By the Errant, this wine is strong... (just quietly, I think I might have a new role going forward)."<br /><br />Moroch Nevath: "I pulled a hammy in the first quarter of the match, and the coach pulled me from the field for the second quarter. I got a bit of ice, and a rub, and came back good as new for the third quarter. I organised the defense in the second half, faced off the opposition captain and made a good show of it, but now I'm wondering who won the damn game?"<br /><br />Kuru Qan: "Was this story a measurable delight? Relevant? Yes!"<br /><br />Turudal Brizad: "I'm too sexy for this shirt...(but really, I just want to be taken seriously don't cha know)."<br /><br />Nifadas: "The role of 'First Eunuch.' Well, let no one say I didn't make a sacrifice for the authenticity of my performance in this role."<br /><br />Gerun Eberict: "Yeah, so I acquired my position by false flagging the King. Bwahahahahaha.... you'd do the same if you could. Admit it. You all want what I've got."<br /><br />Seren Pedac: (Waves hand mysteriously). "'These are not the Crimson Guards you're looking for.' Yeah, I think I can get the hang of this...'"<br /><br />Hull Beddict: "I only did what I had too. It was completely justified by past events. It was a spiritual necessity ... Oh, hi guys, what are you Nerek's here for?"<br /><br />Tehol Beddict: "I nominated Bugg for the best manservant award, his dinners were marvels of inventive resourcefulness."<br /><br />Bugg: "I nominated Tehol for best dressed award. His sartorial excellence is legendary."<br /><br />Shand (speaking with Rissarh and Hejun): "Okay girls, paper, rock, scissors, whoever wins gets the next session with the member from heaven."<br /><br />Ublala Pung: "The bottom line is ... well it crosses my knees ..."<br /><br />Kettle: "I consider this role a promotion from playing a little dutch boy with his finger in a dyke, (and no, don't go there...). Apparently, I've won the 'Cute,' award, and I have no idea how, perhaps it was the way I fed spies and criminals to the Azath... there was so much blood, and it would get into my hair and make it all sticky, and I was dead, and all, but still moving around. Yeah, 'Cute.'"<br /><br />Shurq Elalle: "(ticks off fingers) Stealing scenes, check. Hot, dead chick, check. Got an awesome makeover, check. Ootooloo, check. Okay, fully equipped to kick-ass."<br /><br />Iron Bars: "So, who is this Thanos guy? I hear he's been causing trouble and needs sorting out."<br /><br />And there you have it, another amazing, wonderfully entertaining installment in the Malazan super-epic, monster-stupendous, superlative-superlative [INSERT UNUSED SUPERLATIVE].... (I'm literally out of words) novel.<br /><br /><b>Recommend to anyone who loves to be entertained*. 5 'Best of Marks &amp; Spencer,' stars.</b><br /><br />*Warning - must read books 1 -4 first, lest a spell of confusion and profound perplexity will overtake your mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7341618341685455275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_312980459" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/312980459" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/312980459?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8119976-midnight-tides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer312980459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5344133586192162556">New Continent, new characters, and again a completely new and superior experience on the reread. <br/><br/>This book tells among other things Trull Sengar’s back story. We also learn about the continent of Lether and some of the history of the two superpowers on the continent namely, the Tiste Edur, and the Letherii. We also get a close up view of the forerunner magic system to the warrens – The Tiles and the Holds.<br/><br/>I remember the first time I read this being put out because none of my favourite characters</span>
  <span id="freeText5344133586192162556" style="display:none">New Continent, new characters, and again a completely new and superior experience on the reread. <br /><br />This book tells among other things Trull Sengar’s back story. We also learn about the continent of Lether and some of the history of the two superpowers on the continent namely, the Tiste Edur, and the Letherii. We also get a close up view of the forerunner magic system to the warrens – The Tiles and the Holds.<br /><br />I remember the first time I read this being put out because none of my favourite characters in the series so far were featured. Not only was I cut off from my favourite characters but it seemed I was in a whole new alternate universe to the one I had grown used to. Which makes sense because part of the premise of the story is that the continent of Lether has been isolated and quarantined from the rest of the world, and even from the warren system of magic. <br /><br />This time round it was fun revisiting some of my favourite characters in the series, like Tehol and Bugg, Shurq Ellale and Ublala Pung. The Crimson Guard also feature in the story.<br /><br />Instead of repeating most of what I have already said in my reviews of the previous four books I thought I would have some fun with a few snap shots of life in Letheras.<br /><br />***************************************************************<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Letheras Times</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>World News – Tiste Edur negotiations collapse as god emperor rises. War Imminent</b><br /><br />The Letherii delegation to the Edur led by Crown Prince Quillas was left perplexed as they were witness to a change in Edur leadership brought about by the resurrection of a new king who had recently died in battle. The delegation had hoped to sue the Edur for compensation for the loss of hundreds of harvested seal carcasses that the Edur had confiscated from Letherii ships. The fact that the carcasses were harvested illegally and therefore technically stolen from the Edur was outweighed by the technicality of the harvest still requiring hundreds of man hours to accomplish and therefore requiring compensation. The surrendering of control of Edur fishing grounds was suggested by the Letherii delegation.Things were reported to be going well before the negotiations were abruptly ended by the overthrow of the Edur king AKA The Warlock King, by a resurrected demon covered in Letherii gold coins.<br /><br />The Commander of the Letherii army fronted a press conference earlier today assuring the people of Lether that both the military and the Ceda were mobilising for a tactical response. <br /><br />“We have the army and we have the mages, and we will teach the Edur the meaning of ‘Shock and Awe” when we rain down the magic of the Empty Hold down upon their villages and enslave their children and their children’s children to the tenth generation, for the glory of Lether.”<br /><br />********************************************************************<br /><br /><br /><b>Finance News – Shares in Bugg Constructions up 4000 percent – Technical analysts say company is oversold</b><br /><br />Things are on the up and up for recently floated construction company “Bugg Constructions.” Bugg Constructions share price rocketed in the Tolls after the fledgling company acquired the contract for shoring up the “Eternal Domicile.” Excavations and restoration of the ancient palace had been having trouble with flooding with no solution in sight, threatening to delay the advent of the prophesied “Seventh Closure” when our glorious King Ezgara Diskanar will ascend to take his rightful place on the Empty Throne of the Empty Hold to become the promised god Emperor.<br /><br />Bugg’s Construction demonstrated a secret method of being able to solve the flooding crisis and monies to be received from the works and an ongoing maintenance contract have sent the revenue projections through the roof. <br /><br />The Letheras Times hit the Toll Repository to interview floor traders and frantic investors where they see the share price heading. A well known day trader who preferred to remain anonymous commented<br /><br />“The technical indicators are well into oversold territory, but if you are waiting for a pull back you can forget it. Its just going to keep getting more and more oversold as every man and his dog and the fleas on his dog is just buy buy buying. Hardly anyone’s selling so I don’t know where all these shares are coming from but make hay while the sun shines is my advice.”<br /><br /><br /><b>Finance News - Ratcatcher’s Guild acquires contract for reporting on missing persons</b><br /><br />In the wake of increasing reports of disappearing loved ones in Letheras, the Palace has commissioned the Rat Catcher’s guild to investigate and catalogue all instances of missing persons in the city. When asked about rumours that the Ratcatcher’s Guild was in fact operating secretly as an Assassins Guild, Guild Champion Ormly retorted,<br /><br />“How absurd! Imagine an assassins guild in charge of missing persons. Talk about conflict of interests. Ridiculous!”<br /><br />Indeed.<br /><br /><br />*************************************************************<br /><br /><br /><b>Local News - Well Hung Pung has extra Lung</b><br /><br />The Bookmakers at the canals were in a frenzy today as Ublala Pung survived trial by drowning, walking the bottom of the canal the whole distance with no less than 4300 docks strapped to his back. It turns out Ublala is half Tarthenal and has an extra set of lungs and extra large testicles. Not only could Ublala Pung hold his breath longer, but had extra buoyancy on his side. <br /><br />At 70 to 1 odds Finnad Gerun Ebberict stood most to gain with 800 docks riding on the half caste Tarthenal. Good luck to the Finnad trying to collect on that debt. Bookmaker Turble who held the other end of Gerun’s bet hung himself, kicking over an oil lamp in the process rendering the body unrecognisable. <br /><br />Uh huh...I don’t know about you but this reporter thinks that a little convenient.<br /><br /><br /><b>Local News – Undead Pirate now employing</b><br /><br />Recent survivor of trial by drowning, Shurq Ellale, is planning on celebrating her new existence by graduating from cat burglary to piracy on the high seas. Having already paid for her crimes by dying, Shurq has a virtual “licence to steal” taking advantage of Lether's "double jeopardy" laws preventing her from being killed for the same crime twice. <br /><br />Shurq is kicking off a recruitment drive with a “Pirate Party” where she is hoping to attract the right crew to a career in plunder, pillage and general debauchery. Highly desired are applicants with a degree in beauty therapy specialising in cosmetics for the dead. Barring that, Shurq’s only real requirements in her words ..<br /><br />“So long as you do as I say and are prepared to feed my pet Ootooloo regularly you’re in.”<br /><br /><br /><b>Local News – Vampire apparition stalks Letheras.</b><br /><br />Rumours have surfaced of a silent killer stalking the darkened corners of Letheras at night, ambushing it’s victims and drinking their blood before dragging them away to its lair where it can feed on their cold dead flesh. A tale to scare children into being good? Or do we have a genuine vampire prowling our streets. <br /><br />Reported sightings though varying do share one striking similarity – The vampire or apparition takes the form of a nine or ten year girl, naked, her pale skin smeared, her long hair clotted with coagulating blood. One witness claims to have seen the apparition dragging down a city guard, jumping onto his back and biting into his neck and feeding on his life blood till he was dead. City authorities have advised that people avoid walking alone at night especially in the “seedier” parts of town.<br /><br /><br /><b>Local News - Local Hero helps rescue city from apaocalypse – Now aspires to greater greatness</b><br /><br />Local undead denizen, Harlest Ebberict, claims to have played a crucial role in saving the city from a horde of monsters climbing out of the barrows around the old haunted tower behind the palace. Harlest went into the haunted grounds armed with nothing but his teeth and wit and “mega scariness.” Harlest claims he distracted the creatures by jumping out and “scaring” them into freezing before incapacitating the creatures by “chewing them on the leg” and “clawing their balls off” with his talons. This left his “badass crew” free to move in unopposed to deliver the killing blows without any risk to themselves. <br /><br />We asked Harlest what plans he has for the future - <br /><br />“I want to be a pirate. A scary pirate on a ship of the undead. I want to be scary. It’s important that I be scary. I’ve been practising hissing and snarling.’<br /><br />When asked for a demonstration of scariness Harlest replied with<br /><br />‘Aarrgh! Hiss! Hiss! Hiss—’<br /><br />And admittedly we did indeed piss ourselves...just not with fear.<br /><br />***********************************************************<br /><br />Its 5 stars from me</span>
  <a data-text-id="5344133586192162556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2242550962" />
    <a title="Stefan Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach"><img alt="Stefan Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603215087p2/24053713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2242550962?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bach" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach">Stefan Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8119976-midnight-tides">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2242550962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16996462367009126402"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"There is a tide in the affairs of men and we, at the height, are ready to decline."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>While I'm of an opinion that <i>
  <b>Memories of Ice</b>
</i> is his best <i>
  <b>Malazan</b>
</i> novel, <i>
  <b>Midnight Tides,</b>
</i> with its criticism on materialism and slavery - which in mirroring history <i>(and to a major degree present time)</i> of our own society leaves a sour taste - is probably my favorite book of the series.<br/><br/>Before I could continue with book four, <i>
  <b>House of Chains,</b>
</i> I had to read Midnight Tides, which is fifth in</span>
  <span id="freeText16996462367009126402" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"There is a tide in the affairs of men and we, at the height, are ready to decline."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>While I'm of an opinion that <i>
  <b>Memories of Ice</b>
</i> is his best <i>
  <b>Malazan</b>
</i> novel, <i>
  <b>Midnight Tides,</b>
</i> with its criticism on materialism and slavery - which in mirroring history <i>(and to a major degree present time)</i> of our own society leaves a sour taste - is probably my favorite book of the series.<br><br>Before I could continue with book four, <i>
  <b>House of Chains,</b>
</i> I had to read Midnight Tides, which is fifth installment in <i>
  <b>Malazan Book of the Fallen</b>
</i> series. <br>By doing so, I got introduced myself with all the characters that were active at the same time when story of the first three books happened.<br>It actually makes more sense to read it this way, to switch order of these two books, because now I have a clear path for the story to move forward.<br>So yes, it’s three books of constant introductions of new settings, stories, characters, their histories and philosophies. <br>It’s definitely an expansion and form of exploration of my own.<br><br>So let’s see in which corner of Malazan Earth this book takes us.<br><br>After introducing ourselves with the continents of <i>
  <b>Malazan Empire, Genabackis</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Seven Cities,</b>
</i> we are traveling again to a completely new continent <i>(one of seven in this world),</i> a continent called <i>
  <b>Lether.</b>
</i> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513427999i/24689533._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://atlasoficeandfireblog.files.wordpress.com/2017/12/malazan-world-megamap-with-cities-and-nations.png" rel="nofollow noopener">Link to magnify</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515627516i/24865944._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://vignette3.wikia.nocookie.net/malazan/images/2/2a/Map_Empire_of_Lether.jpg/revision/latest?cb=20101216224647" rel="nofollow noopener">Link to magnify</a><br><br>And it’s really interesting how people and their nations stayed secluded from the rest of the world and within their own borders. <br><br><i>Well, everyone except <i><b>Kingdom of Lether.</b></i></i><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <u>Story.</u>
  </b>
</i><br><br>In its expansion Kingdom of Lether conquered almost all of their bordering nations and now it’s the time to conquer their northern neighbors, not so peaceful <i>
  <b>Tiste Edur</b>
</i> tribes.<br>And the ploy for doing that is quite specific.<br><br>But first we have to understand how Letherii society works.<br>In structure of Letherii society, one can argue, is Erikson’s most plain and obvious criticism of our own history and that still very heavy weight of colonialism and imperialism we are carrying; <br>all while it’s mirroring the contemporary world’s struggle with flaws of capitalism, such as social inequity, exploitation, corruption and greed. <br><br><i>
  <b>“The Letherii motive was, is and shall ever be but one thing. Wealth. Conquest as opportunity.<br>Opportunity as invitation. Invitation as rightful claim. Righteous claim as preordained, as destiny.<br>Destiny as victory, victory as conquest, conquest as wealth. <br><br>But nowhere in that perfect scheme will you find notion of defeat. <br>All failures are temporary, flawed in particular. Correct the particular and victory will be won the next time around.”</b>
</i><br><br>The Letherii society worships wealth. Stacking coins on top of coins – for the sake of stacking coins on top of coins and manic accumulation of that wealth – their true religion. <br>The lack of compassion is being justified by the need to be realistic.<br>Their indebted form of slavery where one’s entire family for generations gets to repay a debt, is bathing in extremity of their judgements. And the fact how they are imposing this to all of their bordering nations is deeply rooted belief of self-righteousness.<br>Life is a contest to be won or lost.<br>Death as arbiter of meaning.<br>And above else, judgement is a thing to be delivered, not delivered unto.<br><br><i>
  <b>“Our headlong progress, as if motion was purpose and purpose inherently virtuous.”</b>
</i><br><br>To the Letherii, gold is all that matters. Its possession defines their entire world.<br>Power, status, self-worth and respect – all were the commodities that could be purchased by coin.<br>Debt bounds the entire Kingdom, defining every relationship and every motivation, every act and decision - hides behind this.<br><br>So, for such nation of belief of grandeur, of predetermination, is completely acceptable that they can intrude foreign territory, to hunt and hoard riches of someone else’s hard labor.<br>And because of their self-righteousness it’s only logical for them - when tribes from whom they have stolen from retaliates and destroys ships, kills the crew and gets back those riches stolen from them - to demand compensation. <br>Not for the ships destroyed, not for the crew killed, but for the loss of the market value they would gain with riches they have stolen in the first place.<br>Thus making yet another nation their indebted slave.<br><br>But this time they are facing Tiste Edurs, who are on the road of self-righteous imperialism and colonization themselves.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <u>Characters.</u>
  </b>
</i><br><br><i>
  <b>"Two sets of brothers."</b>
</i><br><br>Core of this book are <i>
  <b>Bedict</b>
</i> brothers of Lether and <i>
  <b>Sengar</b>
</i> brothers of Tiste Edur, their relationship within each set and differences in their comparison.<br><br><b>It's fascinating to me how dichotomy in which this book started - <br><br></b>when we see three Letherii brothers who don't even hide how estranged they are from each other: <br>‣ where eldest of them <i>
  <b>Hull</b>
</i> is on a mission of redemption and probable betrayal of his Kingdom;<br>‣ <i>
  <b>Tehol,</b>
</i> who despite his genius spends his days penniless on the roof with his manservant <i>
  <b>Bugg;</b>
</i><br>‣ <i>
  <b>Brys,</b>
</i> the youngest brother, who tries to uphold to his duty to his King and Kingdom of Lether for all three of Bedict brothers. <br><br>While on the other side, within closeness of four Edur brothers, vastly different currents run beneath the surface:<br>‣ where, the eldest, <i>
  <b>Fear,</b>
</i> struggles with his duty to his people, to his brothers, to his betroth;<br>‣ <i>
  <b>Binadas,</b>
</i> who runs from his loyalty;<br>‣ <i>
  <b>Trull,</b>
</i> who questions every decision;<br>‣ and <i>
  <b>Rhulad,</b>
</i> the youngest one, who out of inexperience and ignorance can't comprehend the reality of the world <br><br><b>- reversed throughout the book and changed its role within the sets.</b><br><br>We still have that same dichotomy, but completely different relationships of the characters. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <u>Symbolism and Allegory.</u>
  </b>
</i><br><br>After three books heavily oriented on multiple hundreds of people battling each other in close combat in nothing but flesh and bone, with swords, spears and shields, it was a refreshment seeing deployment of magic in war and development of it. <br>Such variety of different types of magic that irreversibly changes the evolution of warfare in this world. <br><br>And even here you can see Erikson’s criticism; this time on weapons of mass destruction. <br><br>When unified tribes and self-proclaimed <i>
  <b>Empire of Tiste Edur</b>
</i> declares war on Kingdom of Lether, Lether King <i>
  <b>Ezgara Diskanar</b>
</i> tries to quickly end the war by ordering his mages to bomb with magic and obliterate all Tiste Edur villages. <br>Under excuse of saving resources and lives of his own troops, which is undeniable truth, Kingdom of Lether saw nothing close to insane in committing genocide and mass murdering of hundreds of thousands of innocent civilians in most undignified way possible: from afar, safely secluded in their borders, dropping magic from the sky above.<br><br><i>
  <b>“This is not war. This is… what? I have no answer to describe the magnitude of this slaughter.<br>It is mindless. Blasphemous. As if we have forgotten dignity. Theirs, our own. The word itself.<br>No distinction between innocence and guilt, condemned by mere existence.<br>People transformed against their will into nothing more than symbols and sketchy representations.”</b>
</i><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <u>Prose.</u>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Following satirical humor from Memories of Ice, I believe of all books in the series, with addition of Letherii fop <i>
  <b>Tehol Bedict</b>
</i> and his manservant <i>
  <b>Bugg,</b>
</i> in this master/servant dichotomy, sarcasm is most prominent in this one here.<br>And while maybe balance of humor and serious observation isn’t as perfect as in <i>
  <b>MoI,</b>
</i> most important thing is that it’s quite enjoyable reading endless battles of wits, in beautifully written satire, between these characters, which again, provides much necessary break from all those mentioned above heavier references.<br><br><i>
  <b>~~~~~</b>
</i><br><br>This is a series where, in my opinion, with every next book Erikson excels even further. There’s seemingly no ending to chasm-like depth of both his worldbuilding and characterization.<br>And it’s such a rewarding series where, after you were depraved of much needed explanations, you get to learn how this world works, but instead to learn such things with those same characters you were following so far in previous books, you get to see how that works on a completely different side of the globe. <br>And when realization strikes and all those bits and pieces you were collecting so far click among themselves, you’ll wish to get back and reread from the beginning.<br><i>(Or you’ll stick until the end and each year get back to reread from the beginning, like some of us here.)</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515628465i/24865955._SX540_.png" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>4.16/5</b>
</i><br><br><i>
  <b>Kharkanas Trilogy<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2167504768?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Forge of Darkness</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462617190?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall of Light</a><br><br>Path to Ascendancy series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464500203?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dancer's Lament</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2189195888?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Landing</a><br><br>Malazan Empire series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1462615386?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Of Knives</a><br><br>Malazan Book of the Fallen series<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203966666?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Gardens of the Moon</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2215973985?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadhouse Gates</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2226844854?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Memories of Ice</a><br><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2181374271?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ultimate Malazan Chronological Reading Order</a></b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16996462367009126402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
