<div id="review_1355757432" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355757432" />
    <a title="Molly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9077850-molly"><img alt="Molly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345305363p2/9077850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1355757432?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Molly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Molly" href="/user/show/9077850-molly">Molly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/13066288-midnight-tides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=steven-erikson">steven-erikson</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9077850-molly?shelf=malazan">malazan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1355757432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4292425228923311839">Rating? Of course, 5 stars ^^<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“This tide is rising, and there are scant few who would stand before it."</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451426763i/17540681._SY540_.jpg' height='666' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“From the twisting, smoke-filled clouds, blood rained down. The last of the sky keeps, flame-wreathed and pouring black smoke, had surrendered the sky. Their ragged descent had torn furrows through the ground as they struck and broke apart with thunderous reverberations, scattering red-stained rocks among the heaps of corpses that covered the land from horizon to horizon. <br/>The great hive c</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText4292425228923311839" style="display:none">Rating? Of course, 5 stars ^^<br><br><b>
  <i>“This tide is rising, and there are scant few who would stand before it."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451426763i/17540681._SY540_.jpg" height="666" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“From the twisting, smoke-filled clouds, blood rained down. The last of the sky keeps, flame-wreathed and pouring black smoke, had surrendered the sky. Their ragged descent had torn furrows through the ground as they struck and broke apart with thunderous reverberations, scattering red-stained rocks among the heaps of corpses that covered the land from horizon to horizon. <br>The great hive cities had been reduced to ash-layered rubble, and the vast towering clouds above each of them that had shot skyward with their destruction – clouds filed with debris and shredded flesh and blood – now swirled in storms of dissipating heat, spreading to fill the sky."</i>
</b><br><br>Erikson sure knows how to get me glued to the book from Prologue to Epilogue.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Chaos needs no allies, for it dwells like a poison in every one of us."</i>
</b><br><br>I approached <i>Midnight Tides</i> with more than a little trepidation (I delayed reading it for two months) because I wasn't sure I was ready for a 900+ pages flashback book (we see the events preceding <i>Trull's shorning</i> from the <i>Tiste Edur</i>, so the events in this one fall before beginning of the fourth book) with no known characters besides <i>Trull Segnar</i> (and the <i>Cripple God</i>).<br><br><b>
  <i>“He studied the hooded figure. ‘I see your problem, you know. I see it now, and curse myself for having missed it before. You have no realm to command, as do other gods. So you sit there, alone, in your tent, and that is the extent of your realm, isn’t it? Broken flesh and foul, stifling air. Skin- thin walls and the heat the old and lame desire. Your world, and you alone in it."</i>
</b><br><br> No <i>Malazans</i>. No <i>Genebackis</i> or <i>Seven Cities</i>. A whole new continent. New places. New faces. Looking at the <i>Dramatis Personae</i>, I was a whining mess. Trull wasn't one of my favorite characters in <i>House of Chains</i> .... he wasn't one of my second or third favorite either ... he was just ... OK. Well, what has to be done, has to be done. I didn't like <i>Karsa</i> in <i>Deadhouse Gates</i> either (or at the beginning of <i>House of Chains</i>) but by the end of the last book he was one of my favorites, so I decided to put my trust in Erikson once again ... <br><br><u>Surprise! Surprise! (not)</u><br><br><u>I loved this book!</u> As mentioned above, I didn't care much for Trull the last time around. Same as I didn't care for the <i>Felisin</i> parts in <i>Deadhouse Gates</i>, or <i>Crocus</i> in in every book except <i>Gardens of the Moon</i>. Here there was harmony, maybe more than in <i>Memories of Ice</i> (and I love that book to pieces)... <u>not one lagging story-line</u>.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Into his heart whispered ... guilt, a ghost and a ghost’s voice, growing monstrous with taloned hands tightening, ever tightening, until his soul began to scream. A piercing cry only Trull could hear, yet a sound that threatened to drive him mad."</i>
</b><br><br> Never boring.The Lether storyline or the Tiste Edur, the Sengar brothers or the Beddict brothers, Rhuald and Trull,<br><br><b>
  <i>“Our brother is doomed to die countless deaths. Die, rise, and die again. Our brother, Fear, the youngest among us. That is how I see it. And now, I am to embrace the power that has done this to Rhulad? I am to serve it? Lend it my skills with the spear? I am to carve an empire for it? <br><br>Are his deaths without pain? Without horror? Is he not scarred? How long, Fear, can his sanity hold on? There he stands, a young warrior bedecked in a gold nightmare, his flesh puckered and mangled, and weapons shall pierce him – he knows it, he knows he will be killed again and again."</i>
</b><br><br> Seren Peddac, Whittal and the Nachts (and the Cripple God), Udinaas the Letheri slave,<br><br><b>
  <i>“Freedom was an altar supplicants struggled to reach all their lives, clawing the smooth floor until blood spattered the gleaming, flawless stone, yet the truth was it remained for ever beyond the grasp of mortals. Even as any sacrifice was justified in its gloried name."</i>
</b><br><br> Tehol and Bugg, Brys Beddict, Ublala, Kettle, Shurq Elalle (and that silly Harlest), Lilac the fisherman demon,<br><br><b>
  <i>“I shall call a healer—’ <br>‘Why? To fight again? To relive terror and grief?’ <br>‘You were not a warrior in your world?’ <br>‘A caster of nets. Warm shoals, a yellow sky. We cast nets.’ <br>‘All of you?’ <br>‘What war is this? Why have I been killed? Why will I never see the river again? My mate, my children. Did we win?"</i>
</b><br><br> ... the two Kenryll’ah princes, and last but not least, Iron Bars and the Crimison Guard (They were new characters, but they had the sweet smell of home, like the Ashok Regiment in the last book). <br><u>Not one dull moment.</u><br><br>We learned of the Letheri,<br><br><b>
  <i>“The notion of inequity, my friends. For from inequity derives the concept of value, whether measured by money or the countless other means of gauging human worth. Simply put, there resides in all of us the unchallenged belief that the poor and the starving are in some way deserving of their fate. In other words, there will always be poor people."</i>
</b><br><br> that saw the world through money and thought themselves destined to rule over everybody not competent enough to amass wealth <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[... and watched their greedy, decadent kingdom crumble. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <i>“Free to profit from the same game. Free to discover one’s own inherent disadvantages. Free to be abused.<br>Free to be exploited. Free to be owned in lieu of debt. Free to be raped.<br>And to know misery. It was a natural truth that some walked that road faster than others.<br>There would always be those who could only crawl.<br>Or fell to the wayside. The most basic laws of existence, after all, were always harsh."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Coin is the poison, after all, and it infects indiscriminately."</i>
</b><br><br> We learned more about the Tiste Edur, and their misplaced believes, the radical change of their ways under a new self proclaimed Emperor.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Sometimes the past rises once again to reveal the lies. Lies that persisted through nothing more than force of will, and collective opinion. Sometimes that revelation comes drenched in fresh blood. Delusions invited their own shattering. Letheri preeminence. Tiste Edur arrogance."</i>
</b><br><br>We found a unique problem of, heh, "overpopulation" in Lether...<br><br><b>
  <i>“the land was twisted by the magic. The dead ... lingered. Here, in the north, and far to the south, as far as Letheras itself. To my mind, an Elder god meddled. But none could have foreseen the consequences, not even an Elder god."</i>
</b><br><br>We discovered <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[gods in disguise...<br><br><b><i>“You are a man of many mysteries, Bugg. Occasional priest, healer, the Waiting Man, consorter with demons and worse. Were I not so self-centred, I’d be intrigued.’ <br>‘I am ever grateful for your self-centredness, master"</i></b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br> We found the reason behind the animosity between the Tiste Andii and the Tiste Edur (oh, that prologue) We met the Tarthenal and have encountered another Forkrul Assail ....<br><br><b>
  <i>“the Edur were gathered. Wills locked in a dreadful war, and, like an island around which the storm raged in endless cycles, the monstrous form of Rhulad Sengar, who had risen from the House of the Dead. Armoured in gold, clothed in wax ..."</i>
</b><br><br> and learned the mystery behind the Nascent, the flooded fragment of Kurald Emurlahn (We waited from the second book through the fourth, and finally the answer is here in the fifth one).<br><br><b>
  <i>“The world felt broken now, irreparably broken."</i>
</b><br><br> We had insight in the "gift" of immortality (courtesy of the Cripple God)..... tasted the bitterness of isolation and loneliness....<br><br><b>
  <i>“Feeling sick, Trull looked away – but there was no direction available to ease him. On all sides, the slowly settling ashes of madness."</i>
</b><br><br>.... and we pawed the way for the story to come.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451426763i/17540682._SX540_.jpg" height="399" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“There was no meaning to be found in lifeless weather, in the pulsing of tides and in the wake of turning seasons.<br>No meaning to living and dying, either. <br>The tyrant was clothed in gold, and the future smelled of blood. <br>It meant nothing."</i>
</b><br><br>Great, often explosive battles (absent in the last book), engaging characters, more background history, more races, more gore and more humor, epic storytelling, social criticism (capitalism , slavery, you name it).<br><br><b>
  <i>“The frightened are ever keen to bow to a perceived necessity, in the belief that necessity forces conformity, and conformity a certain stability. In a world shaped into conformity, dissidents stand out, are easily branded and dealt with. There is no multitude of perspectives, no dialogue. The victim assumes the face of the tyrant, self-righteous and intransigent, and wars breed like vermin. And people die."</i>
</b><br><br>... mind blowing realizations (Ah, that Nascent, that flooding), the destruction of kingdoms (and worlds),<br><br><b>
  <i>“The world had not crumbled, it had shattered, and before his eyes he saw the jagged pieces, a chamber fissured and latticed, a thousand shards bearing countless reflected images. Edur faces, broken crowds, the smear of smoke."</i>
</b><br><br>... the rise of a new Empire, stories of destiny, of humans and gods and of a myriad of other races.... even a hint of badly timed romance. <br><br><b>
  <i>“Fallen. Who tracks our footsteps, I wonder? We who are the forgotten, the discounted and the ignored. When the path is failure, it is never willingly taken. The fallen. Why does my heart weep for them? Not them but us, for most assuredly I am counted among them."</i>
</b><br><br>As always I loved the epic battles, the nuclear devastation left in the wake of the mage cadre and the demons, I cherished those brilliant heroic last stands (<u>nobody does EPIC better than Erikson</u>) but even more (as usual) those small moments of comradery, brotherhood, unlikely friendships, identities lost and found,<br> <br><b>
  <i>“Anguish rose in a flood, burning like acid. As if he had raised his own demon, hulking and hungry, and could only watch as it fed on his soul. Gnawing regret and avid guilt, remorse an unending feast."</i>
</b><br><br>.... little stories, sometimes humorous, often touching. <br><br><b>
  <i>“The end of one thing brought the birth of another, after all. Lives and loves, the gamut of existence was marked by such things. A breaking of paths, the ragged, uneven ever-forward stumble. Blood dried, eventually. Turned to dust."</i>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“The world has drawn breath ... and now breathes once more. As steady as ever, as unbroken in rhythm as the tides."</i>
</b><br><br><u>Riveting! The Bonehunters ... soon.</u><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451472009i/17547330._SY540_.jpg" height="869" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Gulls and sharks, the feast lasting the entire morning. The slave watched, feeling like a spectator before nature’s incessant display, the inevitability of the performance leaving him oddly satisfied. Entertained, in fact. Those who owed. Those who were owed. They sat equally sweet in the belies of the scavengers. And this was a thing of wonder."</i>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4292425228923311839" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2503266762" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503266762" />
    <a title="Veronica " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7035111-veronica"><img alt="Veronica " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360466651p2/7035111.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2503266762?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica " href="/user/show/7035111-veronica">Veronica </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7035111-veronica?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503266762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer625865281734711329"><b>
  <i>Hundreds of millenia, crawling to this shore. The passage of ages is measured by chance. The deep roll of tides, the succession of wayward storms. This is how the world moves - .</i>
</b><br/><br/>If someone told me that the fifth book in a series would have an entirely new cast of characters, veering completely away from the ones with whom readers had become accustomed over the previous four books, I’d say that it was an example of some questionable authorial judgment. Maybe that’s why I’d make a terrible aut</span>
  <span id="freeText625865281734711329" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Hundreds of millenia, crawling to this shore. The passage of ages is measured by chance. The deep roll of tides, the succession of wayward storms. This is how the world moves - .</i>
</b><br /><br />If someone told me that the fifth book in a series would have an entirely new cast of characters, veering completely away from the ones with whom readers had become accustomed over the previous four books, I’d say that it was an example of some questionable authorial judgment. Maybe that’s why I’d make a terrible author, because Steven Erickson certainly proves that making such a move need not be a hindrance to the overall narrative. And when you really get down to it, how else could this massive tale possibly be told? The history of this world stretches back hundreds of thousands of years but it’s not just some old, dusty information confined to a musty book sitting on some long-forgotten shelf. This history is still very much alive and affecting current events, like ripples in water that have stretched out beyond what the eye can see. So even though this particular installment introduces readers to new characters in new settings, it’s still all very connected to everything that’s come before and so, in that sense, there is still a sense of familiarity for readers, a feeling of <i>"I know this"</i>.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>And so it must be. One people. One ruler.</i>
</b><br /><br />Book five in the Malazan series moves the action to yet another continent, one where the human Letherii people have maintained a shaky truce with the Tiste Edur. I won’t say much about the overall plot of the story or the characters introduced along the way. I’ll leave the rush of discovery to readers to enjoy as they move through this exciting tale. I’ll only say that there is one character who will be known to readers and who will be a welcome touchstone anchoring them to the pivotal events as they unfold. And there will be pivotal events because, you see, there’s a prophecy at play and, like most prophecies, what you see isn’t always what you get. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Like hatchlings born on the tide, the peoples of two kingdoms were rushing headlong into deep, deadly waters.</i>
</b><br /><br />If you’re worried that the battle for supremacy between two far-off kingdoms has little relevance to the fights on Seven Cities and Genebackis, to the sacrifices made by brave heroes in the first four books, don’t be. The malignant forces at work beneath the surface of those events are not confined to any one place...or time. In fact, there are a few instances in this book that sync up with the timeline of events in Gardens of the Moon and Deadhouse Gates. So, dear reader, it’s all connected, one thing to the other.<br /><br />Character-wise, Erickson again delivers a plethora of colorful and memorable men and women, drawn from a wide range of races. The main ones, the ones I call tentpole characters, are complex and layered with fully realized motivations, values, and fears. Some are worthy of our respect and admiration. Others deserve our sympathy or pity. And the rest? Well, they warrant the introduction of a two by four to the back of the head. Suffice it to say that these characters draw you in, one way or another. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Death cannot be struggled against, brother. It ever arrives, defiant of every hiding place, of every frantic attempt to escape. Death is every mortal’s shadow, his true shadow, and time is its servant, spinning that shadow slowly round, until what stretched behind one now stretches before him."</i>
</b><br /><br />There is an overall bleak tone to this series thus far and this book is no exception. There is the sense that people, as a whole and regardless of race or culture or time period, all continue making the same mistakes. That they keep falling into the same traps of power - a constant questing for “more”, a never-ending cycle of conquest and destruction. There is so much of this series that is applicable to our real world - the power of greed, the corrupting influence of power itself, the rape of the natural world, the capacity of people to visit pain and misery on others, the tendency of people to stratify themselves (at all levels of society), to just follow along like sheep when they should be screaming objections from the rooftops. It can be disheartening, and yet...and yet...<br /><br />There is still hope, offered through characters who are noble, who attempt to hold true to their friends, family...to themselves, which is sometimes the hardest thing to do. And maybe, in the bigger scheme of the self-feeding cycle of the loss of innocence to baser motivations, it is this clinging to higher ideals - to simply asking the question “why?” - that can be the most heroic act. It is the sisyphean act of choosing to toil away at a hopeless task in the seemingly futile hope of a better outcome, that is, in itself, meaningful.<br /><br /><b>
  <i> Even as he saw the anger grow in the faces of those around him - anger that he dare challenge, that he dare think in ways contrary to theirs, and so threaten their certainty - he was unable to stay silent.</i>
</b><br /><br />I loved the humor in this too because, yes, despite the darker elements of the story there is still light. Erickson always manages to weave in humor, delivering it just when needed. Midnight Tides witnesses the rising of yet another lovable comic duo, though the use of humor is by no means limited to them. I appreciated every chuckle. <br /><br />The ending once again spiralled tighter into itself, like water swirling down a drain, picking up speed and momentum until the end result could no longer be forestalled. Those last several chapters, as people and events were converging, were impossible to put down. I ought to know since I was up until 3 in the morning reading. There were bittersweet moments and I’m left with a sense of urgency to see more of this world, to see where these characters go from here. This is only the halfway mark of the series so there’s still a lot of story left to tell. Given how much Erickson manages to pack into each individual book, I can’t even begin to wrap my head around everything that's still to come.<br /><br /><b>We have come, after all, to the day of the Seventh Closure. An end, and a beginning - </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="625865281734711329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_913944786" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/913944786" />
    <a title="Kaora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora"><img alt="Kaora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542069606p2/7983564.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/913944786?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaora" href="/user/show/7983564-kaora">Kaora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer913944786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6827220778237334797"><i>Tyrants and emperors rise and fall. Civilizations burgeon then die, but there are always casters of nets. And tillers of the soil and herders in the pastures. We are where civilization begins and when it ends, we are there to begin it again.</i><br/><br/>That was amazing.<br/><br/>I think Midnight Tides has become my favorite book thus far in the series.<br/><br/>It is centered around Trull Sengar, whom we met in House of Chains. He and his people the Tiste Edur have been united under the Warlock Kin. However, their time of peac</span>
  <span id="freeText6827220778237334797" style="display:none"><i>Tyrants and emperors rise and fall. Civilizations burgeon then die, but there are always casters of nets. And tillers of the soil and herders in the pastures. We are where civilization begins and when it ends, we are there to begin it again.</i><br /><br />That was amazing.<br /><br />I think Midnight Tides has become my favorite book thus far in the series.<br /><br />It is centered around Trull Sengar, whom we met in House of Chains. He and his people the Tiste Edur have been united under the Warlock Kin. However, their time of peace is coming to an end as war with Lether, a kingdom who has already conquered several other peoples, looms.<br /><br />As always there are some pretty fascinating characters, such as Trull and his brother Fear, and their family servant Udinaas on the side of the Tiste Edur. We also meet some Letherii people, including Tehol Beddit and his manservant Bugg who provided much of the comic relief in this book, as well as his brothers Brys, Hull and various others.<br /><br />Typical Erikson style to give you POVs on both sides of the conflict, so you grow attached to characters that you know may not make it to the end of the book. Yet somehow I just cannot stop reading.<br /><br />I've said it before and I'll say it again. This series takes a TON of work. There is a lot of information here and you will not be spoon fed. However, it makes it so worth it because each book in this series keeps getting better and better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6827220778237334797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_198601932" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198601932" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4162390-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525386186p2/4162390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198601932?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4162390-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8119976-midnight-tides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4162390-lee?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198601932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17238741650860291976">Second time round the only thing that changed from my first read was that I enjoyed it even more! This is still my favourite of the series so far, yet I cannot wait for Bonehunters to start.<br/><br/>Original review below.<br/><br/><b>Story: 5/5</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>1: Being Vague, rambling plot with no little believable storyline<br/>5: Ripping yarn, clever, thought provoking</i>
</blockquote><br/>I must admit to starting this book with some reservation. I had just finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55398.House_of_Chains__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___4_' title='House of Chains (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #4) by Steven Erikson' rel='nofollow noopener'>House of Chains</a> and rated it 5 stars. You can read my review on that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190577990.' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> I was completel</span>
  <span id="freeText17238741650860291976" style="display:none">Second time round the only thing that changed from my first read was that I enjoyed it even more! This is still my favourite of the series so far, yet I cannot wait for Bonehunters to start.<br /><br />Original review below.<br /><br /><b>Story: 5/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Being Vague, rambling plot with no little believable storyline<br />5: Ripping yarn, clever, thought provoking</i>
</blockquote><br />I must admit to starting this book with some reservation. I had just finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55398.House_of_Chains__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___4_" title="House of Chains (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #4) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a> and rated it 5 stars. You can read my review on that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190577990." rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> I was completely ‘into’ the story and the characters of the Malazan world. So when I realised this story was going to be told on a completely different continent with all new characters at a time I was unsure of I was a little hesitant. But Erikson got me again. Another 5 stars. I thoroughly enjoyed the storyline, it was interesting, engaging and I really feel like I got to understand the relatively unknown race of the Tiste Edur. The two main story-lines are based on the Sengar family of Tiste Edur and the Beddicts. Each family has some very interesting characters and drawing the book to a close Erikson completes a thoroughly enjoyable read.<br /><br /><b>Characters: 5/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Unrealistic/unbelievable. Feel nothing for these characters<br />5: Fully engaged with the characters, believable. Researched.</i>
</blockquote><br />Brilliant character development. Powerful, emotional, weird, funny and believable. I had heard so much about Tehol and Bugg that to be honest I was not as impressed with them as I expected to be. Their humour at times became forced and its constant effort to be funny at times became boring. On the other hand the characters Udinaas and Rhulad develop a great relationship that is fully worth reading. Trull Sengar is a rock in this and you do begin to understand the man himself.<br /> <br /><b>Read Weight: Solid</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Fluffy, Light, Solid, Heavy, Struggle</i>
</blockquote><br />So normally Eriksons stuff is Heavy, but this being a standalone, with very little reference to other continents, races, too many gods and ascendents, or 100,000 other characters, it makes is a easier read than normal. Solid it is.<br /><br /><b>Engagement: 4/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Not fussed about finishing<br />5: Could stay up all night</i>
</blockquote><br />I couldn’t wait to get on the train to read it again. I read it at breakfast, I read it at lunch, I even read it walking to the train, but that proved a little to dangerous.<br /><br /><b>Recommend: 4/5</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>1: Would advise you to read something else<br />5: Go read it now. It is THAT good</i>
</blockquote><br />I would recommend this to any Epic fantasy lover, I think that if you hadn’t read other Malazan books you could start with this and get a good understanding of Style of Erikson.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17238741650860291976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2062091883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2062091883" />
    <a title="Sade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16037420-sade"><img alt="Sade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605390492p2/16037420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2062091883?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sade" href="/user/show/16037420-sade">Sade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2062091883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5684479841576091029"><p>
  <br/>
  <i>I honestly panicked when i started reading Book 5. In my mind, i was like, will this be <b>THE</b> Malazan book i officialy have no love for...?Will i ever understand what in the world is going on here? The answer is yes...now i understand why book 5 was more or less a standout book for fans of this novel, you're either going to love it or hate it. I've decided there's no middle ground for Malazan books lol.</i>
  <br/>
  <br/>
</p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Betrayals, more betrayals than any mortal could bear -Feather Witch</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>So b</span>
  <span id="freeText5684479841576091029" style="display:none"><p>
  <br />
  <i>I honestly panicked when i started reading Book 5. In my mind, i was like, will this be <b>THE</b> Malazan book i officialy have no love for...?Will i ever understand what in the world is going on here? The answer is yes...now i understand why book 5 was more or less a standout book for fans of this novel, you're either going to love it or hate it. I've decided there's no middle ground for Malazan books lol.</i>
  <br />
  <br />
</p><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Betrayals, more betrayals than any mortal could bear -Feather Witch</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />So book 5 basically introduces us to new characters, new everything with only one familiar face. It's like you're back in book 1. For the most part, you're like what's happening? who are these people? Time frame wise, i'm thinking book 5 was before the time of Laseen's reign and during Kellanved's reign so basically everything in book 5 precedes Book 1 - I know Erikson loves to show off- <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Characters:</b>
</u> Erikson continues to wow us with more characters to love.. Did you think you could love just the bridge burners or Anomander Rake or Kruppe, Onrack, Icarium, Mappo, Coltaine, Uncle, Duiker, Karso Orlong etc etc etc and not have room for more? Nope, Erikson continues to show that he just wants to give you more characters to love and who he can break your heart with.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Plot:</b>
</u> this is a book that touches on themes of betrayal, vengeance, rise of new civilizations..We're introduced to another one of the Tiste race unlike the Andiis however the Edur's i feel are less in touch with who they really are. It's almost like the story of our favourite Toblakai. There's this re-occurring theme in the Malazan book that without strong knowledge of your history, you're susceptible to lies and being played by men and gods alike.<br /><br />All in all book 5 reads like a beginning of sorts, to new things and i for one i'm totally pumped to continue this journey.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5684479841576091029" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7681816402809296292">okay so i finished it. it took me forever, and it was exhausting, but when i was able to get on a streak of reading, i enjoyed it. its not poorly written, i just have so much difficulty with genre fiction where everything has an unfamiliar name and theres so much dense backstory which, reading midseries, i wasnt privvy to.   <span id="freeText7681816402809296292" style="display:none">okay so i finished it. it took me forever, and it was exhausting, but when i was able to get on a streak of reading, i enjoyed it. its not poorly written, i just have so much difficulty with genre fiction where everything has an unfamiliar name and theres so much dense backstory which, reading midseries, i wasnt privvy to. (fonso said i didnt need to have read any earlier ones, but a customer told me i had been done "a disservice" reading it that way) but thats his reputation - steven erikson - he will just throw you into a world and give you tons of characters and jump you around until you are dizzy. it felt good to have read it, but it feels good to be over, too. i can read other books much faster... </span>

<div id="review_1954433467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954433467" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1954433467?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8119976-midnight-tides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2017">bb-b-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954433467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1451227186976407392"><b>My buddy read of the most complicated series I've ever attempted continues.</b><br/><br/>So just as I was getting into the story of the Malazan empire with the Bridgeburners, New Assendants and New Gods in play we stop and go back thousands of years to before any of the happenings in books 1-4 and start a whole new story with only one character that we have ever seen before. I think I might be dizzy from the abrupt turn about.<br/><br/>This is a story of brothers or two sets of brothers so be more precise. Told mostly </span>
  <span id="freeText1451227186976407392" style="display:none"><b>My buddy read of the most complicated series I've ever attempted continues.</b><br /><br />So just as I was getting into the story of the Malazan empire with the Bridgeburners, New Assendants and New Gods in play we stop and go back thousands of years to before any of the happenings in books 1-4 and start a whole new story with only one character that we have ever seen before. I think I might be dizzy from the abrupt turn about.<br /><br />This is a story of brothers or two sets of brothers so be more precise. Told mostly about the three Tiste Edur brothers Trull is the only character in this book that we have ever seen before. This is the tale of how he was cast out from his people and one of the first power plays made by the Crippled God. On the other side of an upcoming war are the three Beddict brothers. Most of the tale is told from Tehol Beddits perspective and is it an odd yet entertaining one. I found his shenanigans with his loyal servant Bugg to be the best parts of this book.<br /><br />While this book did give some great insight into the past of the Tiste Edur and hints of how things went terribly wrong for them to a point that in the current Malazan books they seem to be mostly killed off it really was my least favorite part of the book. For a few reasons one being that for awhile a lot of the Edur storyline was uncomfortable to read. Rhulad is the younger brother of Trull and Fear and he is so full of pride and envious of everything his brothers are or have. Rhulad flirts with the betrothed of his brother hoping to steal her away and believes himself to be the best warrior but he has never seen a battle. So when he ends up in charge of all of the Tiste Edur everything goes to hell in a handbasket and Trull is the only one to challenge the abomination that is Rhulad.<br /><br />Tehol’s chapters are much lighter in tone and have a plethora of interesting characters. Bugg his faithful manservant that can make dinner out of just about anything was one of my favorites. Then there is a little corpse girl wandering around killing random people here and there and I loved her. <br /><blockquote>
  <i> ‘Kettle, how many people have you killed in the past year?’<br />She cocked her head. ‘I can’t count past eight and two.’ <br />‘Ah.’ <br />‘Lots of eight and twos.’</i>
</blockquote><br />Just remember to be her friend and you should be fine. I’m not sure what Tehol’s revenge on the city was going to be but it seemed like he was trying to take down the entire Lethori culture. It just so happened to end up coming to a head at the end when the Tiste Edur show up to fight the Lethori and something else is breaking free of it’s chains all at the same time.<br /><br />There are some great characters in this and I was a little wowed to find out what/who Bugg is. But then at the same time at the end of this I had no idea why we have an entire book dedicated to the history of this world and wondered will we see many of the characters from this in future books because I believe there are millennia inbetween. I guess at this point in time I really didn’t see a point to it.<br /><br />Still the storytelling is vast and intricate and I feel like I’m only catching the tip of the iceberg and getting 10% of the story while there is another 90% going on underneath that I’m totally missing. These books are truly dense and I must go slowly since it take complete concentration. There are many other same story lines going on at the same time with so many other characters that I really just can’t comment on everything happening.<br /><br />I’m excited to get back to the main storyline and see how anything from this book plays into the present day events. There are a few characters that I would really like to see again like Iron Hands, Bugg, Tehol, Udinaas and Feather Witch. And who knows in this series it is entirely possible that they show up again with a new name and a new agenda.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1451227186976407392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2682349552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2682349552" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7467113-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600867751p2/7467113.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2682349552?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/7467113-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7467113-mark?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7467113-mark?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2682349552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18303136230992753057">Another excellent installment in the Malazan series. At first, I did not think I was going to like this as much as previous volumes; it was a new setting and almost all new characters. But I allowed myself to be emerged in the story at hand, and while it’s a very different one, it is just as strong as the preceding books.<br/><br/>Midnight Tides is a study in contrasts, as we have one society (the Letherii), who are obsessed with forward progress and capitalism, pitted against a very different society (th</span>
  <span id="freeText18303136230992753057" style="display:none">Another excellent installment in the Malazan series. At first, I did not think I was going to like this as much as previous volumes; it was a new setting and almost all new characters. But I allowed myself to be emerged in the story at hand, and while it’s a very different one, it is just as strong as the preceding books.<br /><br />Midnight Tides is a study in contrasts, as we have one society (the Letherii), who are obsessed with forward progress and capitalism, pitted against a very different society (the Tiste Edur) who cling to the traditions of the past. When a certain event shakes up the Tiste Edur, we begin to witness this clash of cultures. <br /><br />There is also quite a bit of philosophical waxing in this book, along with commentary on economics. <br />And, while Erikson has always employed gallows humor in this series, the level of humor and absurdity here seems greater than before, almost akin to his “Bauchelain and Korbal Broach” novellas. Much of this is due to the characters Tehol and his manservant Bugg, who have a relationship similar to that of P.G. Wodehouse’s Wooster and Jeeves.<br /><br />I would also like to mention Trull. This is a character who I was mostly indifferent to in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/55398.House_of_Chains__Malazan_Book_of_the_Fallen___4_" title="House of Chains (Malazan Book of the Fallen, #4) by Steven Erikson" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Chains</a>, but after reading his backstory, I absolutely love the character. It will be interesting to go back and re-read HoC at some point, now that I have this new perspective and understanding of who he is. <br /><br />As for the conclusion...well, it is pretty intense, as has become a hallmark of Erikson’s writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18303136230992753057" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wEdyJtvjgYNBX8IqtysU5oTHe3oJ+V7hXejsiVsbMiOzkfm/DYZTNPsFigr04EIJt8+yzSTT4k94wDpceOayfw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2KL3zZMmSQi3f9zJt/pGQy3+v2xGUPCieI9H+zKW4uWrdHxURUObvw0llOn0MRCsHvZ222t6TAxdp5EuEWtiuQ==')})
  }
//]]>

For there is a new Emperor on the throne of Malaz, and he is dwelling on the ignominy that is the Empire\'s failed invasion of the Korel subcontinent. In the vaults beneath Unta, the Imperial capital, lie the answers to that disaster. And out of this buried history surfaces the name Stonewielder. In Korel, Lord Protector Hiam, commander of the Stormguard, faces the potential annihilation of all that he holds dear. With few remaining men and a crumbling stone wall that has seen better days, he confronts an ancient enemy: the sea-borne Stormriders have returned. Religious war also threatens these lands. The cult of the Blessed Lady, which had stood firm against the Riders for millennia, now seeks to eradicate its rivals. Her victories have made her popular - a shade too popular for her employer\'s taste. Betrayed, thrown down a mountain and left for dead, Murcatto\'s reward is a broken body and a burning hunger for vengeance. Whatever the cost, seven men must die.\n\nHer allies include Styria\'s least reliable drunkard, Styria\'s most treacherous poisoner, a mass-murderer obsessed with numbers and a Northman who just wants to do the right thing. Her enemies number the better half of the nation. And that\'s all before the most dangerous man in the world is dispatched to hunt her down and finish the job Duke Orso started...\n\nSpringtime in Styria. And that means revenge.\n<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"17726791479402527078\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div Sha\'ik is dead. One last rebel force remains, holed up in the city of Y\'Ghatan and under the fanatical command of Leoman of the Flails. The prospect of laying siege to this ancient fortress makes the battle-weary Malaz 14th Army uneasy. For it was here that the Empire\'s greatest champion Dassem Ultor was slain and a tide of Malazan blood spilled. A place of foreboding, its smell is of death. But elsewhere, agents of a far greater conflict have made their opening moves. The Crippled God has been granted a place in the pantheon, a schism threatens and sides must be chosen. Whatever each god decides, the ground-rules have changed, irrevocably, terrifyingly and the first blood spilled will be in the mortal world.
